Title: TWG XXXVIII: Dessert Planet Horror Wolves Win
Post by: Haplo on March 04, 2013, 07:50:51 PM
Your spaceship has crash landed on an unknown desert planet. You and the rest of the colony were sent to start inhabiting a new planet, unfortunately, this is not the planet you were intended to land on. Everyone panicked after waking up from stasis. Many never even woke up. More died as you tried your best to survive the harsh conditions. However, one woman stepped up to the plant. Her name was Epp. Thanks to Epp, you folk have managed to figure out a way to live on this planet, making use of ship parts and the natural environment. You've worked out a temporary solution that should last for several, and are merely waiting for a passing spaceship to see your beacon.

Things were looking great, however all was not well. The planet's atmosphere must have affected some of your crew mates. You wake up to find that Haplo had been viciously murdered in the night. You all cry out to Epp and ask her what you should do about the murder. Perhaps, not quite right in her own head, Epp determines that you must all decide to vote on who the murderer is and then she will execute that person at sundown. She then secretly assigns 3 players to be her guards, in order to watch her back at night. And thus begins your little colony's 2nd fight for survival.

There are a few unique rules, so please read them

Rules
1. Epp is the Leader. She has 3 abilites.
     A. Epp is a confirmed Human.
     B. Epp cannot be night killed while a guard still lives.
     C. If there is a tie for a lynch when day ends, Epp will choose between one of them to kill(she can choose to kill someone she didn't vote for if she wishes).
2. After the day has ended there is no night talking. Only Epp may post in the thread, and only if there is a tied vote, in which she will choose which to lynch, there can be no trying to sway her decision after night has been called.
3. There are 3 guards to start with. When a guard dies, they will be revealed as a guard.
4. If the psychos(wolves) attempt to assassinate Epp at night while a guard lives, 1 living wolf at random will be revealed upon daybreak.
5. Each day, eveyone will vote on 1 player to lynch. At the end of the day, Epp will execute whoever has the most votes.
6. Wolves win by killing Epp, throwing the colony into chaos.
7. Humans win by killing all the wolves.
8. Unlimited votes
9. 48 Hour days and 24 Hour nights.
10. Days/nights will start/end at 10pm EST.
11. You may not post the contents of your PM(you can still make claims, but your not allowed to post the wording in order to attempt to gain an advantage.

Player List.
1. AngryNarwhal Lynch D1
2. Epp
3. Guy
4. Reaper
5. Modi Thursday Killed N2
6. AJ Lynch D2
7. Iron
8. Dietcar Killed N1
9. Phil Lynch D3
10. Deathbutt Killed N4 G
11. Big Bird Killed N3 G
12. Trientalis Lynch D4

All PMs have been sent. If you somehow did not receive one. Please let me know.

Title: Re: TWG XXXVIII: Desert Planet Horror Day 1
Post by: Modi Thorson on March 05, 2013, 04:00:06 PM
I don't think it's a very good idea to reveal a lot about who is/isn't a guard. This game is pretty tricky. If we focus on one person and accidentally reveal that they are a guard, the psychos move quite a bit closer to their goal. If we spread our accusations out, eep might reveal enough about who ISN'T a wolf to give the wolves a pretty good idea of what's going on. Both of these are pretty extreme - we obviously don't all decide to accuse the same person simultaneously, but we also don't all accuse completely different people.

But whatever the case, I think it's better to focus on people that have been accused rather than random people. Not that Epp actually said much by suggesting that Trientalis MIGHT be a guard, but it's pretty sensitive information overall.

Phil asking about guards didn't strike me as particularly unusual. However, I think he asked if there was a seer, which I would be more prone to consider rolefishing.

Quote from: AngryNarwhal on March 05, 2013, 03:15:48 PM

If you're a vanilla, take one for the team, do not risk setting the lynch onto a real guard and forcing THEIR claim. I am in fact seriously wondering if it would be a good idea to lynch a volunteer today.

I keep misinterpreting lynch as night kill. I agree that claiming guard to avoid the lynch is not the best idea, unless you can be sure that it will move onto a wolf - it might otherwise move the lynch onto a REAL guard. However, claiming guard to draw the NK away from the real guards would be a conceivable idea if someone could do it without sounding really dumb, since a real guard would probably not claim under normal conditions.

Title: Re: TWG XXXVIII: Desert Planet Horror Day 1
Post by: guy on March 05, 2013, 10:42:53 PM
-losing guards is bad. lynching guards is awful.
losing a guard is not the same thing as losing a seer or a guardian in any other twg. it's worse and we should try to prevent it as best we can while looking for wolves.

-losing vanillas is less bad than usual. we have a confirmed human that can't die (eep) that also decides ties. wolves would need to outnumber all of us to control anything, which probably isn't a reasonable thing to be afraid of

-lynching vanillas is not necessarily a bad thing, or even counterproductive. the amount of good that we're missing out on by not lynching a wolf is not nearly as much as the amount of bad we're preventing by not lynching a guard. we have time on our side, i think. there are probably more people the wolves need to kill (3+1 known) than we need to kill (?how many wolves). lynching a guard is really bad and everyone learns immediately that they were guard. this is probably more helpful knowledge to the wolves than the humans; they can relax a little. lynching a wolf is great, but we have time. lynching a vanilla is not that bad

-these are all additional reasons why guards in danger of being lynched should claim. and that we should think very carefully about whether or not to believe them and not just immediately learn towards disbelief just because wolves can do it too

-using activity as a basis for lynching is as productive as random lynching. possibly less since an inactive guard could prove beneficial, as eep pointed out (wolves won't think to or won't want to nk)

another thing i just thought of that is fundamentally different is that we're ALWAYS aware of how close the wolves are to winning. we always know how many of their targets are alive. i think this is another reason missing an opportunity to lynch a wolf is less bad, and a reason it's okay to leave guard claims alive, even if more likely wolf than guard (still/always a chance they're truthful). and, as everyone has pointed out- wolves are likely to guard claim too. so we'll probably have a good idea of how many wolves we've gotten (if a claim isn't revealed as guard, they're probably wolf). we can always keep track of the progress of the game and use that to our advantage. we'll always know how dire it is at the moment to kill them.

additionally and somewhat contradictory, this is a reason for wolves to not claim guardian, so that they're numbers are less well known, and because of that further reason to listen to guard claims, as there is NO downside to guards in danger of being lynched to claim.
(guards will always claim, wolves MIGHT claim)


my thoughts still seem too convoluted. i'm positive it's logically sound so someone help me out maybe

Since Dietcar was killed in the night, it seems unlikely that he was a wolf protecting his kindred. I do agree that we have very little against Phil at the moment, and I think we ought to be able to make a fairly well informed decision tonight. Phil remains a safe vote, but we still want to lynch a psycho if we can.

The wolves can be clever, though. There could very well be a wolf vote on Narwhal, even if Narwhal was a wolf. If there are three wolves, then only myself, Narwhal, Epp, Iron, Dietcar, and Trient voted for other people. Azrael did not vote. Epp is a confirmed human, and Narwhal and Dietcar are both dead, which leaves Iron, Trient, and Azreal (excluding myself, obviously - I suppose this logic does not apply as well to everyone's perspectives). So if Narwhal wasn't a wolf, then all three of those must be wolves, which seems highly unlikely, and even if he was, most of the possible pairings between those three don't seem very feasible. We can draw speculation from this, perhaps, but there was probably at least one wolf on Narwhal.

The order of the votes matters. If it looks like a hopeless case, a wolf could vote for kindred just to appear to be on the opposite team as that person. This wasn't a particularly hopeless case, though, so I'm not sure why a wolf would vote for Narwhal.

Ok... so what can we take out of the nightkill then?  I really am torn between whether this was wolves targeting Trient by adding suspicion onto her or if Trient is a wolf and getting rid of a threat.

Take this as you will, but here's my take on the wolves' picking strategy.

In this game, wolves NEED to kill guards. It's not a matter of simply trying to stay under cover and reach dominance through numbers. They have to do a great deal of hunting to try to find the guards in a sea of vanillas (and eep) trying to protact their guards. If I HAD to guess why Danny was killed it was because they thought he, out of all players, was likely a guard. There may have been some other reasons (day voting, interaction with others) but these would be secondary to their primary goal of selecting a guard. They can dissect the day any which way, but they CANNOT win until the guards are gone, and they can NK eep. The longer they dawdle, the longer they spend not winning. I've been going through the game with the assumption we are dealing with four wolves, because this game seems very tipped in our favor unless they have considerable numbers.

In this game, wolves NEED to kill guards. It's not a matter of simply trying to stay under cover and reach dominance through numbers. There may have been some other reasons (day voting, interaction with others) but these would be secondary to their primary goal of selecting a guard. Title: Re: TWG XXXVIII: Desert Planet Horror Day 2
Post by: Phil on March 09, 2013, 10:59:57 AM
Quote from: epplant on March 09, 2013, 10:43:38 AM
i feel like perhaps we are being too cautious about not outing guards, and this is preventing us from outing wolves

I wholeheartedly disagree.

I'm going to write out two scenarios in which we get rid of all the vanillas and the wolves fail to nk a guard at any point.

Scenario 1:
Four wolves, Three guards, Epp left standing
D1: Votes tie up, epp decides kill, wolf dies.
N1:Wolves pick a guard
D2: Three wolves, two guards, Epp. Votes tie, epp decides, wolf dies
N2:See N1
D3:Two Wolves, one guard, epp. Vote ties, epp decides, wolf dies
N3:See N1
D4:One wolf, epp. Vote ties. Epp Decides, human win

Scenario 2:
Three wolves, three guards, Epp remaining
D1: Epp and guard lynch a wolf
N2: Wolves kill a guard
Repeat until no more wolves. Humans win.

As long as we have all our guards alive, we have no reason to attempt to out guards, as either game scenario is a win for us. I wouldn't worry about really buckling down until we lose our first guard.

Title: Re: TWG XXXVIII: Desert Planet Horror Day 2
Post by: Iron on March 10, 2013, 06:28:58 PM
I think your biggest disadvantage, Tri, is that there is not much else presenting itself for lynch candidacy.

It's really hard to push for an inactive to get lynched, because there are few arguments against them personally.


10 players. 7 are active. Exactly 3 are guards. ~3 are wolves. Eep is the leader.

Lynch a non-eep player at random. You have a ~33% chance of hitting a wolf (assuming we have killed none) and exactly a 33% chance of hitting a guard. This is neat because it means we have exactly a 66% chance of hitting a nonguard. Furthermore, guards can claim (vanillas can't, wolves can but will be punished if it fails to work).

Lynch an inactive player at random (AJ, Reaper, Modi). Those same ratios apply - 66% chance of not hitting a guard. Probably about 33% of hitting a wolf; same for guard. Guard can also speak up for themselves - if they don't, they weren't contributing anything but a number anyway.

The only real risk is if someone like AJ is not reading, is a guard, and gets lynched before claiming. We'll still know he was a guard, but too late to save him. Not too late to use the info.



So in this game, where lying low is rather different than usual, perhaps we have more incentive than normal to hit an inactive (something I'm usually in favor of anyway). That said, lynching someone who you really think is a wolf is obviously way better, so if your gut screams Tri or Phil, that's fine too.

Title: Re: TWG XXXVIII: Dessert Planet Horror Day 3
Post by: Iron on March 12, 2013, 07:55:37 PM
Phil-human-seer gets a big advantage from claiming because he outed a wolf. That one is obvious.

Phil-wolf-seer gets a big advantage because he kills two or more known guards at the cost of only one wolf.

Phil-wolf-vanilla gets a big advantage because he kills one known guard (deathbutt) and/or determines the identity of me when I confess I'm a guard or disclaim him (in the latter case they still must NK deathbutt).

It's a Xanatos gambit - no matter if he is right or wrong, no matter his alignment or role, wolves come out ahead.



Average, lynching no guard claimaints, assuming we have a little less than 2 average wolves.
D3 (Today): We have 7 maybes.
Lynch a nonguard.
Begin N3: 6 left, 3 guard, 1.5 wolves, 1.5 humans.
Lose 0.66 of a guard.
Begin D4: 5 left. We have 2.3 guard, 1.5 wolves, 1.2 humans.
Lynch a nonguard.
Begin N4. 4 left. We have 2.3 guards, 1 wolf, 0.7 humans.
Lose 0.7 of a guard.
Begin D5: 3 left. We have 1.5 guards, 1 wolf, .5 humans.
Lynch a nonguard.
Begin N5: 2 left. We have 1.5 guards, 0.3 wolves, 0.2 humans
Begin D6: 1 left + eep
Probability of Eep being alive: 100%
Probability of a single guard being alive: 60%
Probability of a wolf being alive: 30%
Probability of an additional human being alive: 10%


As you can see, the less guards there are, the better the wolves are doing. This also generously assumes we've killed a wolf.

 Our biggest advantage is delaying the killing of a guard the longest we can afford to, until we really think we have a guard-claimant wolf. This should be obvious even without numbers, objectively (which is more what I mean by mathematically, I suppose).

Even if you don't like the probability thing, you can still see from DB's decision trees that similar things will go down.

TL;DR - More guards = longer survival = more chance of killing wolves.

It makes SENSE to kill wolves that are not masquerading as guards unless you are VERY CONFIDENT, and I don't see why you'd be so confident.


Basically everyone keeps assuming that I'm a guard, so it's not weird that deathbutt did the same.

Title: Re: TWG XXXVIII: Dessert Planet Horror Day 4
Post by: Mystic on March 20, 2013, 11:32:16 PM
one action can have more that one perspective

the wolves don't care which wolf you lynch, they care about winning. the only possible win they could have would be to control the vote, which would be caused by the extremely unlikely split vote from the humans. therefore they had to convince the humans, somehow, to split the vote. this is what happened.

objectively, you changed your vote to reaper.

you saw one wolf over another wolf. you were convinced to vote for a different wolf.

they saw split vote. you were convinced to give iron or them control of the vote. iron didn't take it, so they successfully pulled off their only goal.

Title: Re: TWG XXXVIII: Dessert Planet Horror Day 4
Post by: eep on March 21, 2013, 07:04:58 AM
at least on day 1, i think the wolves got put at a disadvantage because of poor play. it isn't that absurd, no matter what the set-up, to believe that the guards would know whether i knew their identity, and even if not, phil could have asked haplo rather than me. so i gave an ambiguous answer that made guard knowledge of this clear.

guy was put in the spotlight because he misinterpreted my answer as "yes, me and the guards know each other," became outraged because he thought haplo had fucked the balance, and responded as such. if he had stopped to notice the ambiguity of my response, or just kept quiet in thread and raged at haplo directly, then he wouldn't have been caught.

they did a good job of saving after it happened, but i could have done this with any or no information in the right circumstances. bluffing, and the ability to respond to bluffs without outing yourself, is part of the game, on both sides.

Title: Re: TWG XXXVIII: Dessert Planet Horror Day 4
Post by: Mystic on March 21, 2013, 07:17:58 AM
Quote from: epplant on March 21, 2013, 07:04:58 AM
guy was put in the spotlight because he misinterpreted my answer as "yes, me and the guards know each other," became outraged because he thought haplo had fucked the balance, and responded as such.

er no i don't think this is what happened.

they did screw up by calling attention to it, but the fact remains that you still easily could know non-guards and IF they hadn't deflected it away, you could have feasibly figured out all of the guards by asking particular questions about something only they saw. it's not just about your bluffing, it's that you actually had real confirmation. it would be fine and awesome play if you were just pulling that stuff out of nowhere. but i know that you weren't.

i think too many people get excited to write flavor/send out pms and don't realize how silly that will often make the game. i'm reminded of the h2g2 twg on fb that was basically awful in that regard, iirc.

i often spend weeks on writing the flavor, then reading and re-reading them to make sure that the pms i'm sending out won't inadvertently break the game. it's frustrating to see people not put that much effort into it. it's also unfortunate that i don't like to and don't want to run a vanilla game, so the actual effort i put into that part of play doesn't end up being very useful since the mechanics themselves end up being tailored to the wrong audience.

anyway i want encourage writers to really keep in mind what they are doing and not let the excitement of controlling your flavor and setup to ruin your chances of actually running the game fairly. even the most simple of mechanics can and will be broken by lazy pm work or other unclear rules. PLAY THROUGH YOUR GAME a few times with many different scenarios to see what happens. a couple of test runs with semi-random votes would have found the tiebreaker issue in this game extremely quickly.

i mean, it was a good attempt at fixing the "ties" problem (which we don't really have a good way around yet, but this also lets each host put their own mark on the game) but ended up being quite problematic.

Quote from: epplant on March 21, 2013, 08:28:59 AM
Not inherently, no. it would have been broken if i knew who the guards were, or if the guards knew that themselves. i don't see how explicitly knowing something that most players assumed for themselves anyways is broken.

Just because something more broken exists doesn't mean that the first thing isn't bad. I think the first problem here is that you're assuming most players assume something about the game. Title: Re: TWG XXXVIII: Dessert Planet Horror Wolves Win
Post by: eep on March 21, 2013, 04:30:09 PM
No, you aren't really understanding it.

If we lynch a guard claimant, and they are telling the truth, then we reduce the number of guards by 1, as well as giving the wolves an opportunity to kill another guard entirely. If we lynch a vanilla instead, then the wolves are either forced to keep a guard alive (at risk of killing a vanilla), or kill the person we want them to. If we lynch a guard claimant and are wrong, we could go from 3 guards to 1 in a single cycle. Not worth it.

Case in point: if people had gone through with lynching death butt when he was being hella wolfy, humans would have lost the game then and there, despite there being a number of reasons to believe him to be such.

Also saying that we only killed one wolf under the guidance of a wolf is actually not an argument for anything.
